📃 Summary: Last name of the individual
🎨 Patterns:
  • [A-Z][a-z''-]+
    Last names typically start with a capital letter and are followed by lowercase letters. Some names may include hyphens or apostrophes.
  • [A-ZÀ-ÖØ-Þa-zà-öø-ÿ''-]+
    A more permissive pattern that allows for unconventional names or potential data errors.

📃 Summary: Local phone number
🦄 Unique: This column represents the local phone number of the individual taxpayer. For this table, each row is for a unique taxpayer. Phone numbers are typically unique for each individual, and in this case, they appear to be distinct across the sample rows.
🎨 Patterns:
  • \d{3}-\d{4}
    Phone numbers in the format of XXX-XXXX, where X represents a digit

city
▲
not_null

📃 Summary: City of residence
🎨 Patterns:
  • [A-Z\s'']+
    Uppercase city names, possibly with spaces or apostrophes
  • ^[A-Z\s]+-\*$
    City names ending with "-*"
  • ^[A-Z]+(?:[\s-][A-Z]+)*$
    Full city names with possible hyphens
  • ^.*$
    Any text (to cover special cases)

Cocoon Cleaning Summary 🤗


📃 1. Table Summary


The table is about individual taxpayers. It contains personal details like name, gender, contact information, and location. Financial information includes salary, tax rate, and exemptions. Marital status and presence of children are also recorded. This data is likely used for tax calculation and demographic analysis purposes.

🚧 3. Erroneous Values


🔍 4 columns have erroneous values
  1. city: 'NEW YORK' and 'BROOKLYN' represent the same city. 'SAINT LOUIS' and 'SAINT PAUL' use different formats than 'ST. PETERSBURG'.
    ❌ The column has not been cleaned

  2. state: 'AK-*' is unusual because it's not a standard state abbreviation and includes a special character.
    ✔️ The column has been cleaned:
    Original Value Cleaned Value
    0 AK-* AK

  3. single_exemption_amount: '0-*' is unusual because it's not a numeric value like the others and its meaning is unclear.
    ✔️ The column has been cleaned:
    Original Value Cleaned Value
    0 0-* 0
    1 20 2000
    2 40 4000
    3 87 0
    4 103 0
    5 110 0
    6 159 0

  4. child_exemption_amount: '0-*' is not a clear numeric value. Very low amounts like '20' or '40' seem unusually small for exemptions.
    ✔️ The column has been cleaned:
    Original Value Cleaned Value
    0 20 2000
    1 40 4000
    2 159 1590
    3 103 1030

    4855 KILGORE 69216
    4856 HILLIARD 43026

    Explanation: For each value in 'city', there possibly is a unique value in 'state' and 'zip_code', but not necessarily in 'single_exemption_amount', 'married_exemption_amount', or 'child_exemption_amount'. Here's the reasoning: 1. State: Generally, a city is located in only one state, so this relationship is likely one-to-one. 2. Zip code: While it's possible for a city to have multiple zip codes, in many cases, especially for smaller cities, there may be only one zip code. This could potentially be a one-to-one relationship, but it's not guaranteed for all cities. 3. Exemption amounts (single, married, child): These are likely to be set at a state or federal level, not at a city level. Multiple cities within the same state would likely have the same exemption amounts. Therefore, these are unlikely to be in a one-to-one relationship with city.
